    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_621be76d-432d-406b-8bdc-2bbb0971cca0'

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_430242'><a id="like_count_community_question_430242" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/430242?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13415554-the-assassin-and-the-pirate-lord">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/11744704-lauren---seriesous-books"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1430592290i/11744704._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/11744704-lauren---seriesous-books">Lauren - SERIESous Books</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You don't have to, though it provides insight into Celaena's character. She's quite jaded in Throne of Glass and some people find that off putting bec<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You don't have to, though it provides insight into Celaena's character. She's quite jaded in Throne of Glass and some people find that off putting because they don't know her backstory. I found that reading the novellas first let me understand Celaena's outlook on life and her personality, allowing me to enjoy Throne of Glass a lot more since I wasn't becoming frustrated with her nonchalant attitude. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

Sam gave me so many feels in a span of one novella than Rowan ever did in two books. On top of that, I just love the chemistry between Sam and Celaena. Sorry Rowan! :P</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3140472968755802684"><u>3 STAR'S</u> <br/><br/><i>“Come on, Sardothien,” he said, slinging an arm around her shoulders. “If you’re done liberating slaves and destroying pirate cities, then let’s go home.”</i><br/><br/>Well, this was a really really slow first novella... The beginning was pretty boring but the last couple of chapters when everything went down was really good. I did still enjoy it for the most part but at the same time, it fell a little short. It could have been so, so, much better! Anyway, I'm loving getting an inside look into Celae</span>
  <span id="freeText3140472968755802684" style="display:none"><u>3 STAR'S</u> <br><br><i>“Come on, Sardothien,” he said, slinging an arm around her shoulders. “If you’re done liberating slaves and destroying pirate cities, then let’s go home.”</i><br><br>Well, this was a really really slow first novella... The beginning was pretty boring but the last couple of chapters when everything went down was really good. I did still enjoy it for the most part but at the same time, it fell a little short. It could have been so, so, much better! Anyway, I'm loving getting an inside look into Celaena's past and getting the chance to fall in love with Sam Cortland even though I know what's coming and it's gonna break my heart 😭. I already really like his personality and can see his appeal. Celaena, it was nice to see things haven't changed all that much haha. She's still cocky, brave, do anything for her friend, witty and of course <b>Vain</b> as hell. I love the assassin but I gotta say I love the Queen even more so. As for Rolfe, I was NOT impressed. Like. At. All. I wanted more from his character, needed more. I don't feel like it really added anything new to his character :( Welp this was a good start looking forward to starting <i>The Assassin and the Healer</i>. <br><br> <i>“Sam smiled, his brown eyes turning golden in the dawn. It was such a Sam look, the twinkle of mischief, the hint of exasperation, the kindness that would always, always make him a better person than she was.” </i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538464009i/26387113._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Embracing Sam was different, somehow. Like she wanted to curl into his warmth, like for one moment, she didn't have to worry about anything or anybody.”</i></span>

  <span id="freeText13109718181403159336" style="display:none">Q:<br />Quiet as mice, quiet as the wind, quiet as the grave. And she does.</b><br />Q:<br />Thankfully, her sleepwear was as exquisite as her daytime wardrobe—and cost nearly as much. I told you I was beautiful.” (c)<br /><br /><b>And some nifty 'best hiding places are in plain site' ideas:</b><br />Q:<br />What better place to hide than in the middle of the capital city? (c)<br />Q:<br />A little intimidation never did any harm. (c)<br />Q:<br />All that the world knew about Celaena Sardothien, Adarlan’s Assassin, was that she was female. And she wanted to keep it that way. How else would she be able to stroll the broad avenues of Rifthold or infiltrate grand parties by posing as foreign nobility? (c)<br /><br /><br /><b>And she's got quite a tongue on her:</b><br />Q:<br />“You’re assassins,” she growled at him. “You’re supposed to be able to retrieve a body without being seen.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“If I’d been there, I would have killed all of them to get Ben’s body back!” (c)<br />Q:<br />“He can’t be a very good lord,” she said, “if this is his personal office.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I suppose you don’t need an introduction.” Rolfe turned to her.<br />“No.” Celaena leaned back farther in his desk chair. “I suppose I don’t.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Get out of my chair.”<br />... “You really need to work on organizing this mess.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“How long, exactly, have you been involved in the slave trade?” (c)<br />Q:<br />“I’m the world’s greatest assassin.” She lifted her chin. “I’m not afraid of anyone.”<br />“Really?” Rolfe asked. “Because I’m the world’s greatest pirate, and I’m afraid of a great number of people. That’s how I’ve managed to stay alive for so long.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Why go to so much trouble for slaves?”<br />“Because if we don’t fight for them, who will?” (c)<br /><br /><b>Nifty:</b><br />Q:<br />The map—that was the mythic map that he’d sold his soul to have inked on his hands. She breathed it in, staring across the leagues of lonely, black ocean, seeing, somehow, that distant city that had once, long ago, been her home. The wind ripped the strands of hair from her braid, lashing them across her face. Orynth. A city of light and music, watched over by an alabaster castle with an opal tower so bright it could be viewed for miles.<br />The moonlight vanished behind a thick cloud. In the sudden dark, the stars glowed brighter. (c)<br />Q:<br />Somewhere near the back, one of the mountain men began translating. And then two others translated, too—one in the language of Melisande, and another in a language she didn’t recognize. Had it been clever or cowardly of them not to speak up last night when she asked who spoke the common tongue? (c)<br /><br /><b>And she has some interesting plans:</b><br />Q:<br />“No matter if the chain is still up, no matter what might be happening in town, the moment the sun slips over the horizon, you start rowing like hell.” (c)<br />Q:<br />...she tripped a passing pirate, who spilled his drink on an already belligerent man, who in turn tried to punch him in the face but hit the man next to him instead. By luck, at that moment, a trick card fell out of a man’s sleeve, a prostitute slapped a pirate wench, and the tavern exploded into a brawl. ... <br />Animals...<br />To her delight, the streets weren’t much better. ...<br />“ENOUGH!”<br />Everyone lifted whatever they had in their hands—a mug, a sword, a clump of hair—and saluted.<br />And then promptly resumed fighting. (c)<br />Q:<br />It didn’t take much to get away from a group of half-drunk battlecrazed pirates. (c)<br />Q:<br />She’d … she’d … Well, she’d kill him if he was dead. (c)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12876010905011336564"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>The other day, I got a comment on one of my reviews for the <i>Throne of Glass </i>series. A stan had decided to tell me that the only reason I didn't like the books was because I hadn't read the <i>prequels</i> yet. My reaction was, "Are you kidding me? I've read books 1-7, and yet I <i>still </i>need to read more books in this series after clocking in around three thousand pages to give this series a fair shot?" I said as much. The stan did not respond.<br/><br/><br/><br/>I'v</span>
  <span id="freeText12876010905011336564" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>The other day, I got a comment on one of my reviews for the <i>Throne of Glass </i>series. A stan had decided to tell me that the only reason I didn't like the books was because I hadn't read the <i>prequels</i> yet. My reaction was, "Are you kidding me? I've read books 1-7, and yet I <i>still </i>need to read more books in this series after clocking in around three thousand pages to give this series a fair shot?" I said as much. The stan did not respond.<br><br><br><br>I've been told that the prequels are allegedly better than the main novels, but if that's the case, their charm is lost on me. Teenage Celery is just as annoying as adult Celery. We see her here as a sixteen-year-old assassin, and very proud of the fact that she doesn't really kill anyone, so much as kick, punch, shove, and insult them while also bragging about how beautiful and great she is. The only other person I know with so much confidence and so little credibility is Donald Trump.<br><br><br><br>Celery's mission is to go to the pirate lord Rolfe to see him about his slave trade. She's very angry about the fact that he has so many slaves, but doesn't kill the pirate lord - nor does she see the correlation between assassin and slave trader; like him, she is also a robber of lives, only when you're dead, there's no chance of freedom. No, <i>she's </i>got the moral high ground here. Right. *side-eye*<br><br><br><br>I thought this book was just as lame as the other books, personally. But I got the anthology edition of these short stories from the library (ironically, the day after I received that stan comment), so I assume that it's fate that I must read these. Who knows? Maybe one will sway me.<br><br><br><br>Stranger things have happened.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>

<div id="review_1393063631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1393063631" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1393063631?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15713897-the-assassin-and-the-pirate-lord">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393063631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10608085527217802007">What an incredible start of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b>!<br/><br/>This novella made me admire the notorious assassin <b>Celaena Sardothien</b> more. Her character here is far more well-developed compared to her character in <b>Throne of Glass</b>. In this novella, her bad-assery can easily be perceived. She’s <b>braver, more dangerous</b>, and a <b>lot more ferocious</b> than I’ve ever thought. Sarah J. Maas has really given us a firecracker of a female main character!<br/><br/>The <b>Assassin and the Pirate Lord</b> is the first novella of <b>The Assassin’s </b></span>
  <span id="freeText10608085527217802007" style="display:none">What an incredible start of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b>!<br /><br />This novella made me admire the notorious assassin <b>Celaena Sardothien</b> more. Her character here is far more well-developed compared to her character in <b>Throne of Glass</b>. In this novella, her bad-assery can easily be perceived. She’s <b>braver, more dangerous</b>, and a <b>lot more ferocious</b> than I’ve ever thought. Sarah J. Maas has really given us a firecracker of a female main character!<br /><br />The <b>Assassin and the Pirate Lord</b> is the first novella of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b>. It’s a flashback story of Celaena’s past, particularly before she was captured by the Crown Prince of Adarlan <b>Dorian</b> and the Captain of the Guard <b>Chaol</b>. It was such a great experience discovering Celaena’s past, getting to know the people she was acquainted with, like her master– <b>Arobynn Hamel</b> and of course, her childhood close friend who soon turned her love interest, <b>Sam Cortland</b>. This novella also apparently featured the Pirate Lord himself, <b>Rolfe</b>.<br /><br />What I love about this novella was how the action scenes carried me away. It was a blast! And Celaena completely blown me away with her fierceness. Her heart is so soft but she kills without hesitation! <b>THIS IS WHAT I’M LOOKING FOR IN A CELAENA SARDOTHIEN!</b><br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10608085527217802007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Sam was wonderful; I loved him from first glance and his back-story still breaks my heart. It was weird being actually introduced to Sam, because his memory has played such a big part in the series, it has just felt like I've always known him.           <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780731874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16076600941996996083">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin'</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16076600941996996083" style="display:none">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br><br>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin's Blade</b>. And because I love <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J_Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas's</a>
</b> story telling and her writing, I am going to go ahead and read these beauties.<br><br>So, with that said, I am going to read and rate these so I can finally be completely caught up on The Throne of Glass Series: Throne of Glass, Crown of Midnight, Heir of Fire, Queen of Shadows, Empire of Storms, and Tower of Dawn.<br><br><u>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord (Throne of Glass, #0.1)</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512943987ra/24649174.gif" alt="" width="350" height="147" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What an introduction my dear Captain Rolfe, Lord of the Pirates. I now understand why you hate Celaena so much and might I say, it is pretty funny. And might I add, you are the absolute worst kind of person.<br><br>If an assassin, the most feared I might add, and her colleague, Sam, are disgusted with even the idea of slaves, then what is your excuse Rolfe? <br><br>I mean really, you walked into the mess that is Celaena. She may be an assassin, but she has good intentions. She may love throwing temper tantrum, but always be aware that she has something more dramtic up her sleeve for you. <br><br>This was a lovely novella. It sheds a lot of light on Empire of Storms, and why The Pirate Lord was being such a baby about things. <br><br><b>I would encourage anyone reading this series to read the novellas before Empire of Storms to save you any confusion.</b><br><br>P.S. I already love Sam and I already know my heart is going to hurt when I am done with these novellas.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9580101267597583984">Actual rating: 3.5 :)<br/><br/>I have not read the Throne of Glass series, but I enjoyed Ms. Maas's 'A Court of Thorns and Roses' and wanted a quick read, so I picked up this novella.<br/><br/>I have tried not to mention any specific plot-points, but if you have not read this novella and would like to go into it completely blind, then there might be some spoilers ahead. So please read at your own discretion. :)<br/><br/>Characters:<br/><br/>I found it very difficult to appreciate the protagonist, Calaena. I tried very hard to understa</span>
  <span id="freeText9580101267597583984" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5 :)<br /><br />I have not read the Throne of Glass series, but I enjoyed Ms. Maas's 'A Court of Thorns and Roses' and wanted a quick read, so I picked up this novella.<br /><br />I have tried not to mention any specific plot-points, but if you have not read this novella and would like to go into it completely blind, then there might be some spoilers ahead. So please read at your own discretion. :)<br /><br />Characters:<br /><br />I found it very difficult to appreciate the protagonist, Calaena. I tried very hard to understand her, but her words and actions depicted her as incredibly self-righteous, arrogant, self-centered, rude, ill-tempered, and rather naive. Ironically, these are traits I actually adore in most characters, as long as they are offset with a bit of humility, or vulnerability. Now, I can completely understand the type of person one would need to be in order to excel as an assassin, but I found nearly all of Calaena's speeches, thoughts, and actions contradictory. She would boast (endlessly) about being the most lethal (and beautiful) assassin there is, and yet she did not kill anyone in this novella (in situations which you could argue truly called for her to do so). There was even a line saying: "After all, she was an assassin, not a murderer," which prompted me to look up the dictionary definition of both words:<br /><br />Murder: 'the killing of another human being.'<br />Assassin: 'a murderer, especially one who kills a politically prominent person for fanatical or monetary reasons.'<br /><br />Hmm... According to Calaena, herself, she is an assassin, not a murderer. So... does that mean she gets paid for <i>not</i> killing people? I confuse.<br /><br />I think I would have warmed up to her much more if she put her money where her mouth is. It could very well simply be a pet-peeve of mine, but I find it frustrating when a character claims to be a certain way, and yet none of their actions support it. It's just bragging.<br /><br />I found Sam by far the most realistic and rational character. However, I could not understand how Calaena, who would not 'allegedly' hesitate to kill him should he even look at her the wrong way, was all of a sudden gravely concerned for his survival/well-being. And this brings me to the biggest qualm I had with this novella, Calaena's sudden pang of morality and justice:<br /><br />Not once during the entire book did Calaena display any shred of humanity towards anyone. No comradery, no kindness, no vulnerability. There was not even the smallest spec/throw-away line/back-story/joke/anything that would indicate that she is capable of altruism, and yet she becomes so consumed by this sudden need to free an anonymous band of slaves that it makes her character completely implausible. For someone as arrogant and self-important as the protagonist, someone who is supposed to be a ruthless killer with no regard for human life, or for the well-being of even her own friends/allies, she is so quick to risk her life to liberate people she owes no allegiance to. If she was portrayed as someone with a soft spot for slaves, or someone who used to be enslaved, or knew someone who suffered from slavery, or if she had shown even the smallest shreds of compassion towards anything or anyone, perhaps I would be more invested in her mission.<br /><br />I felt that the way she challenged people was identical, regardless of who was on the receiving end. It didn't matter if she was conversing with Sam (with whom she grew up), or a pirate lord twice her age (with whom she was conducting business). This depicted her as tactless, and her crude language and arrogance did not help validate her character. Instead of giving her credibility as a ruthless assassin they depicted her as a naïve child who does not understand consequence.<br /><br />The Writing:<br /><br />One of the first things I noticed was how the book 'feels' as though it was written from an omniscient point of view. On multiple occasions, I would be reading about multiple character's impressions of an event within the same paragraph, which was quite disorienting. <br /><br />I also found the usage of nouns and pronouns rather confusing. A sentence would be speaking of a male character (Sam), and then refer to 'she', and 'her' in the remainder of the sentence. This would force me to go back and re-read the same sentence in order to understand whom exactly the author was speaking of.<br /><br />Too many times a conversation is interrupted by long expositional thoughts. It's perfectly acceptable to incorporate backstories (in short bursts of paragraphs) into the story while the character is walking from A to B, or awaiting someone's arrival; not so much when these expositional paragraphs are forced in-between sentences spoken during a fast conversation. It felt as though after each sentence, the story would be paused for the character to provide exposition through her thoughts/memory flashbacks, which really disrupted the flow.<br /><br />There are far too many references to modern language which made the story less plausible. Words like 'bathroom', instead of latrines. Or phrases like 'get ready to unleash hell' instead of 'prepare to unleash hell'. Or using modern slang like 'make out' something in the distance, instead of 'detect' something in the distance. The language sounded a bit cartoonish at times: "He was so mad, he practically had steam blowing out his ears", and it felt a bit lazy at other times, like "tying down <i>various things</i> before the storm hits."<br /><br />With all that said, I must say I really enjoyed Ms. Maas's descriptions of scenery. They are incredibly vivid and alive, and always paint such incredible detail in my mind with so few words. Here are just a few examples of what I loved:<br /><br />"Fat drops of rain splattered on the rust-colored earth, instantly cooling the muggy air."<br />"Rain lashed out against the shutters, muffling the clink of her cup against the saucer."<br /><br />In conclusion, I must say I enjoyed this read. It was short and sweet, and a great appetizer prior to the main course of Throne of Glass. I'm not sure whether the questions raised in this novella (like the moving map on Rolfe's hand, Arrobyn's real reason for sending a masked Calaena to conduct 'trade', why Ben was killed, etc.) will be answered in the upcoming novellas, but I think if there had been a more solid resolution (or a small hint towards one), I would've rated this story higher. I do think this is a wonderful book and that Sarah J Maas is a wonderful writer, and if you like a quick adventure, you should definitely check it out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9580101267597583984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282079533" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4177529176051548471">**Re-read on September 22nd-23rd, 2015:<br/><b>Actual rating: 3.5/5 stars</b><br/>I personally think the novella wasn't as good as the first three books from the series. Celaena Sardothien was 16 years old in this book and at that time, Sam Cortland was still alive, but I couldn't tolerate her gargantuan arrogance at all! Although I did better understand the story plot after reading the sequels first this time, her impossibly terrible attitude was the most dislike part for me. <b>
  <blockquote>“One day,” Rolfe said, too quiet</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText4177529176051548471" style="display:none">**Re-read on September 22nd-23rd, 2015:<br /><b>Actual rating: 3.5/5 stars</b><br />I personally think the novella wasn't as good as the first three books from the series. Celaena Sardothien was 16 years old in this book and at that time, Sam Cortland was still alive, but I couldn't tolerate her gargantuan arrogance at all! Although I did better understand the story plot after reading the sequels first this time, her impossibly terrible attitude was the most dislike part for me. <b>
  <blockquote>“One day,” Rolfe said, too quietly, “someone’s really going make you pay for that arrogance.” Lightning made his green eyes flicker. “I just hope I’m there to see it.”</blockquote>
</b> Honestly, I have to agree with Rolfe here. For the very first time I'd love to see you suffer for your bossiness, Celaena.<br />The only reason I gave it one more star was because I could relate to the characters more during the re-read and everything made sense.<br /><br /><br />**Reading for the first time on May 19th-21st, 2015:<br /><b>Initial rating: 2.5/5 stars</b><br /><i>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</i> is a novella of the <i>Throne of Glass</i> series and I initially thought it'd be a great book. After a few pages of reading, I started to get bored by the main character, Celaena Sardothien's attitude and behavior. I mean, she was just a 16-year-old girl and she acted way too mature. Just because she was trained to be a professional assassin or protégée doesn't mean she had to be that mature. I don't like the arrogance in her tone whenever she talked to the Pirate or the fellow assassins and I didn't have the same level of excitement in the fighting scenes or her killing skills as I always gained in other novels. </span>

<div id="review_356566934" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356566934" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338449051p2/1489224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356566934?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356566934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14840052179789565566">After hearing so many positive things (prior to publication) about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_' title='Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Throne of Glass</a>, I was expecting a lot from the first prequel, <i>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</i>, and boy was I disappointed. I typically have little to say about short stories and novellas—just read my embarrassing attempts at writing a review for the various short-story collections I've read—but there is a lot to say about this one and none of it is positive. <br/><br/>This story was a miss in terms of writing and characterization. The no</span>
  <span id="freeText14840052179789565566" style="display:none">After hearing so many positive things (prior to publication) about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, I was expecting a lot from the first prequel, <i>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</i>, and boy was I disappointed. I typically have little to say about short stories and novellas—just read my embarrassing attempts at writing a review for the various short-story collections I've read—but there is a lot to say about this one and none of it is positive. <br /><br />This story was a miss in terms of writing and characterization. The novella was filled with grammatical errors and awkward sentences that were hard to follow even when they were grammatically correct. The dialogue was unrealistic and often times cheesy. This was a classic example of telling instead of showing. Not only was there a lot of telling, much of what is told is actually contradicted by what is shown. For example, we're told Celaena is a good liar but throughout the story she constantly casts suspicion on herself by her failure to disguise her true feelings. Overall, the writing was very juvenile even for young adult literature.<br /><br />Even more problematic was the characterization. We're supposed to believe that the protagonist, Celaena, is the most fearsome assassin in the world, yet she doesn't actually kill anyone in the novella despite having ample opportunity and no shortage of enemies. Instead she renders her opponents unconscious by hitting them on the head with the pommel of her dagger (because she's "an assassin not a murderer"—her explanation not mine). She admits to killing people for adultery but finds it morally questionable to kill slave traders, which makes absolutely no sense. She doesn't even kill the main villain despite the fact that he has zero redeeming qualities and he gives her no reason to spare him. In addition to her failure to kill anyone, I found Celaena to be very unlikable. She is bratty, vain, smug, and foolish. Her personality made it even more difficult to believe she was a skilled assassin. <br /><br />After reading this novella, I am no longer excited to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>. My only hope is that these issues were improved upon by more careful editing in the novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14840052179789565566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16167120760222636306" style="display:none">The Assassin and the Pirate Lord wasn't my first glimpse into the world of Throne of Glass that author Sarah J. Maas has created. <div id="review_305383312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305383312" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781599909547" href="/book/show/13419885-the-assassin-and-the-pirate-lord">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">readers of YA genre and adventure books.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=novella">novella</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305383312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11666246029977098804">I had waited quite a long time to read a good story about an assassin heroine. Sarah J. Mass certainly didn't disappoint me. <br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Why?” Sam stepped close enough that she needed to tilt her head back to see his face. “We’re assassins. We kill people. We destroy lives every day.”<br/><br/>“We have a choice,” she breathed.</i>
</blockquote><br/>The assassin is Celaena Sardothien, a sixteen years old teenage girl. Her age was the only thing that <i>cute</i> about her. Celaena is the best assassin that Assassin’s Guild have. She's beautifu</span>
  <span id="freeText11666246029977098804" style="display:none">I had waited quite a long time to read a good story about an assassin heroine. Sarah J. Mass certainly didn't disappoint me. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“Why?” Sam stepped close enough that she needed to tilt her head back to see his face. “We’re assassins. We kill people. We destroy lives every day.”<br><br>“We have a choice,” she breathed.</i>
</blockquote><br>The assassin is Celaena Sardothien, a sixteen years old teenage girl. Her age was the only thing that <i>cute</i> about her. Celaena is the best assassin that Assassin’s Guild have. She's beautiful and deadly, such qualities that make oh-so-arrogant aura sticks with her most of the times. I better not giving details about the story since this is a novella. Any kind of information about the story might be too much. So the big picture is about Celaena and her partner Sam doing an assignment which involved the pirates and slavery. I must say I enjoyed it very much. The first half was spent without action while the last half was full of actions. Though, I can't say I was bored reading the first half. The characters, by this I mean Celaena and Sam, were intriguing. As I said earlier, we have a strong but very arrogant and icy heroine. Celaena is the kind of young girl with huge ego because she's aware that she's very good despite her very young age. I had disliked her at the beginning, before she started to reveal her compassion for others. Sam, on the other hand, is everything that Celaena is not. He's friendly, talkative, calm, and reachable. With these two assassins like fire and ice doing a mission together, how could I get bored?<br><br>Albeit the fact that <i>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</i> is a debut, I liked the writing. My only complaint was the story is told from third person pov, but I felt it was being told from first person pov. Everything was described through Celaena, which of course wasn't supposed to be that way. Although it annoyed me, the writing was good enough to get me hook and drew my emotions. There were some touching moments between Celaena and Sam. Though their relationship was more like brother-sister thing rather than a romance fling (despite I got the hints that Sam -probably- had a deeper feeling for Celaena), I liked both of them together.<br><br>As the first novella, the very beginning story of <i>Throne of Glass</i> series, this was a good one. <i>The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</i>, has successfully rocked my expectation for the series. If I don't read the second novella soon it won't be because I don't want to, but because the third novella: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13419891-the-assassin-and-the-desert?utm_medium=api&amp;utm_source=blog_book" rel="nofollow noopener">The Assassin and the Desert</a> isn't published yet. I'm very curious with the series right now and I'm not comfortable with waiting. Therefore, dear author, the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527-throne-of-glass?utm_medium=api&amp;utm_source=blog_book" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> novel needs to be published sooner than the schedule on August... please?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374003ra/727890.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11666246029977098804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_277708713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277708713" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7756593-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277708713?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/7756593-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277708713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12921403574861010833">So I remember vaguely remember reading Queen of Glass (now Throne of Glass) on fictionpress years ago, like when I was in high school, and I remembered being extremely impressed with the idea of Cinderella as an assassin. I only read the first part of the story, so I can only give my opinion of the first part. The story and idea was wonderful and creative, but the writing definitely needed some improvement. <br/><br/>I was rather excited for this novella because I was interested in the story, but I also h</span>
  <span id="freeText12921403574861010833" style="display:none">So I remember vaguely remember reading Queen of Glass (now Throne of Glass) on fictionpress years ago, like when I was in high school, and I remembered being extremely impressed with the idea of Cinderella as an assassin. I only read the first part of the story, so I can only give my opinion of the first part. The story and idea was wonderful and creative, but the writing definitely needed some improvement. <br /><br />I was rather excited for this novella because I was interested in the story, but I also hoped that Ms. Maas had improved her writing to do justice to the beautiful world she had created. However, after reading this novella, I was slightly disappointed. Her writing style is rather simple and slightly plain. I'm not expecting lyrical and beautiful prose you might expect from, say Patricia A. McKillip, but I do expect an author to be able to set a mood for me to feel. Unfortunately, in the novella, alot of the scenes fail to make me feel anything for the characters. For example, the very first opening scene would have been great if I could feel the suspense and tension between the characters, but I felt nothing. Feelings and mood were stated in words rather than described, which would be the more effective route. <br /><br />I also had a slight problem with our main heroine, Celaena Sardothien. I love the idea of a kickass heroine that has a backbone of steel, but Celaena seems a bit naive, don't you think? I don't want to spoil anything, but I do think Celaena's actions in this novella really made her seem unrealistically naive. To be an assassin, one must be able to cast aside ALOT of moral principles that normal people hold to. The assassins' guild Celaena belongs to is described as the best. Being the best, especially in the field of killing people for money, carries with it an understood ruthlessness. I expect coldhearted murder from my assassins, not some moral highground. Also, Celaena mentions that her guild only goes after the "bad" people (greedy aristocrats, etc.). I would like to point out that what she said doesn't make much sense. If the assassins only kill the bad people, who do you think hire them? The good guys? No, if you're a good guy, you don't hire assassins to kill your enemy BECAUSE you're the good guy, the honorable person who would never do such a thing. So back to that question, who do you think is hiring the assassins? Also, if you assassinate people as a profession, chances are, sooner or later some poor innocent bastard will accidently witness the act, what do you think you have to do? Even if the person is innocent, you probably have to kill him/her. So this moral highground that Celaena expresses in this novella confused me. It doesn't seem to fit a person in such a profession. <br /><br />To wrap up this long rant, I don't exactly think the novella is the worse book ever, but I also don't think it's very good. It's in the "meh" category. I don't regret reading it, but I also don't love it (and I really really wanted to love it). <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12921403574861010833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_755085141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755085141" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755085141?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755085141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8939078317115310522">Celaena was a little bit of a brat in the beginning. However her drive to protect her friends is still there and you can see that she really is a strong woman even from someone so young.<br/><br/>The cute interactions with Sam are fun. She almost flirts by threatening and it is so her. Even now she has such a strong sense of morality for an assassin and I find that refreshing. <br/><br/>This is a really good look into her beginnings and her relationship with the Assassin Lord. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bG7tl1m5dvNnxcNWJxm417EclT+NVvjvPNUpHOtj43CGnCZGWP4Jm7zKSFcFZWly94UktR9b1MjfqTITbEmwcg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FLhUeaXdsbjaGU6a+sRL/8fk9HHsHJ7+YXoz7h0lGlH+Sp+opJrO0AEWxZvYuJpagX1F+34RstmCBijhmg9JUw==')})
  }
//]]>
